<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Environment of Ivory Coast">Environment of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Politics of Ivory Coast">Politics of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg/250px-Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bd/Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bd/Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="276" data-file-height="183" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Force_special_ivoirienne.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Special_forces" title="Special forces">Special Forces</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">Military Operations</a> unit of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Forces_of_the_Ivory_Coast" title="Republican Forces of the Ivory Coast" class="mw-redirect">Republican Forces of the Ivory Coast</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1983, Ivory Coast's capital has been <a href="/wiki/Yamoussoukro" title="Yamoussoukro">Yamoussoukro</a>. <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a> is the administrative center. Most countries maintain their embassies in Abidjan. The Ivoirian population continues to suffer because of an ongoing civil war. International human rights organizations have noted problems with the treatment of captive non-combatants by both sides and the re-emergence of child slavery among workers in cocoa production.</p>
<p>Although most of the fighting ended by late 2004, the country remained split in two, with the north controlled by the <i>New Forces</i> (FN). A new presidential election was expected to be held in October 2005, and an agreement was reached among the rival parties in March 2007 to proceed with this, but it continued to be postponed until November 2010 due to delays in its preparation.</p>
<p>Elections were finally held in 2010. The first round of elections were held peacefully, and widely hailed as free and fair. Runoffs were held 28 November 2010, after being delayed one week from the original date of 21 November. <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Gbagbo" title="Laurent Gbagbo">Laurent Gbagbo</a> as president ran against former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Alassane_Ouattara" title="Alassane Ouattara">Alassane Ouattara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 December, the Electoral Commission declared that Ouattara had won the election by a margin of 54% to 46%. In response, the Gbagbo-aligned Constitutional Council rejected the declaration, and the government announced that country's borders had been sealed. An Ivorian military spokesman said, "The air, land and sea border of the country are closed to all movement of people and goods."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Foreign relations of Ivory Coast">Foreign relations of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>Ivory Coast is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" title="La Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">La Francophonie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Military of Ivory Coast">Military of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>As of 2012, major equipment items reported by the Ivory Coast Army included ten <a href="/wiki/T-55" title="T-55" class="mw-redirect">T-55</a> tanks (marked as potentially unserviceable), 5 <a href="/wiki/AMX-13" title="AMX-13">AMX-13</a> light tanks, 34 reconnaissance vehicles, 10 BMP-1/2 armoured infantry fighting vehicles, 41 wheeled APCs, and 36+ artillery pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012 the Ivory Coast Airforce consisted of one <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">Mil Mi-24</a> attack helicopter and three SA330L Puma transports (marked as potentially unserviceable).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Economy of Ivory Coast">Economy of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="862" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cote_d%27Ivoire.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Ivory Coast's exports.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ivory Coast has, for the region, a relatively high income per capita (USD 1014.4 in 2013 ) and plays a key role in transit trade for neighboring, landlocked countries. The country is the largest economy in the <a href="/wiki/West_African_Economic_and_Monetary_Union" title="West African Economic and Monetary Union" class="mw-redirect">West African Economic and Monetary Union</a>, constituting 40 percent of the monetary union’s total GDP. The country is the world's largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">Cocoa beans</a>, and the fourth largest exporter of goods, in general, in sub-Saharan Africa (following South Africa, Nigeria and Angola).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, the cocoa bean farmers earned $2.53 billion for cocoa exports and is expected to produce 630,000 metric tons in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/The_Hershey_Company" title="The Hershey Company">The Hershey Company</a>, the price of cocoa beans are expected to rise dramatically in upcoming years.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The Ivory Coast also has 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber" class="mw-redirect">rubber</a> farmers which earned a total of $105 million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The maintenance of close ties to France since independence in 1960, diversification of agriculture for export, and encouragement of foreign investment, have been factors in the economic growth of Ivory Coast. In recent years Ivory Coast has been subject to greater competition and falling prices in the global marketplace for its primary agricultural crops: coffee and cocoa. That, compounded with high internal corruption, makes life difficult for the grower, those exporting into foreign markets, as well as for the labor force in as much as instances of indentured labor have been reported in the cocoa and coffee production in every edition of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" title="U.S. Department of Labor" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Labor</a>'s <i>List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</i> since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Demographics of Ivory Coast">Demographics of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abidjan2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Abidjan2.jpg/600px-Abidjan2.jpg" width="600" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Abidjan2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Abidjan2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="802" data-file-height="281" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abidjan2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a> with an estimated population of 4.6 million in 2014 is the Ivory Coast's largest <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">settlement</a> and the economic capital of the Ivory Coast.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The country's population was 15,366,672 in 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and was estimated to be 20,617,068 in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> and 23,919,000 in July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Republic_of_C.C3.B4te_d.27Ivoire_National_Statistical_Institute_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_C.C3.B4te_d.27Ivoire_National_Statistical_Institute-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Ivory Coast's first national census in 1975 counted 6.7 million inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to 2012 government survey, the <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" title="Fertility rate" class="mw-redirect">fertility rate</a> was 5.0, with 3.7 in urban areas and 6.3 in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Languages of Ivory Coast">Languages of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>French, the official language, is taught in schools and serves as a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> in the country. An estimated 65 languages are spoken in Ivory Coast. One of the most common is <a href="/wiki/Dioula_language" title="Dioula language" class="mw-redirect">Dyula</a>, Bete which acts as a trade language as well as a language commonly spoken by the Muslim population.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ethnic groups include <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> 42.1%, Voltaiques or <a href="/wiki/Gur_languages" title="Gur languages">Gur</a> 17.6%, <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9_peoples" title="Mandé peoples">Northern Mandes</a> 16.5%, <a href="/wiki/Kru_people" title="Kru people">Krous</a> 11%, <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9_peoples" title="Mandé peoples">Southern Mandes</a> 10%, other 2.8% (includes 30,000 Lebanese and 45,000 French; 2004). 77% of the population are considered Ivoirians.</p>
<p>Since Ivory Coast has established itself as one of the most successful West African nations, about 20% of the population (about 3.4&#160;million) consists of workers from neighbouring Liberia, Burkina Faso and Guinea.</p>
<p>4% of the population is of non-African ancestry. Many are French,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Lebanese,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Vietnamese and Spanish citizens, as well as Protestant missionaries from the United States and Canada. In November 2004, around 10,000 French and other foreign nationals evacuated Ivory Coast due to <a href="/wiki/2004_French%E2%80%93Ivorian_clashes" title="2004 French–Ivorian clashes">attacks</a> from pro-government youth militias.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Aside from French nationals, there are native-born descendants of French settlers who arrived during the country's colonial period.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tr style="background:#ddd">
<th colspan="5">Religion in Ivory Coast<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></th>
</tr>
<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
<td style="padding:0 4px;">Religion</td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>

<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Ivory_Coast" title="Religion in Ivory Coast">Religion in Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>The native born population is roughly split into three groups of Muslim, Christian (primarily Roman Catholic) and <a href="/wiki/Animist" title="Animist" class="mw-redirect">animist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Religion in Ivory Coast remains very <a href="/wiki/Heterogeneity" title="Heterogeneity" class="mw-redirect">heterogeneous</a>, with Islam (almost all <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Muslims</a>, with some <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadi</a> Muslims<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>) and Christianity (mostly Roman Catholic with smaller numbers of <a href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists" class="mw-redirect">Methodists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants" class="mw-redirect">Protestants</a>) being the major religions. Muslims dominate the north, while Christians dominate the south. In 2009, according to U.S. Department of State estimates, Christians and Muslims each made up 35 to 40% of the population, while an estimated 25% of the population practiced traditional religions.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ivory Coast's capital, Yamoussoukro, is home to the largest church building<sup id="cite_ref-BOLPY_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOLPY-79"><span>[</span>n 6<span>]</span></a></sup> in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Peace_of_Yamoussoukro" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Peace of Yamoussoukro" class="mw-redirect">Basilica of Our Lady of Peace of Yamoussoukro</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Ivory_Coast" title="Health in Ivory Coast">Health in Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was 41 for males in 2004; for females it was 47.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-80"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">Infant mortality</a> was 118 of 1000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-80"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> There are 12 physicians per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-80"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> About a quarter of the population lives below the international poverty line of US$1.25 a day.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> About 36% of women have undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> According to 2010 estimates, Ivory Coast has the 27th highest <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality" class="mw-redirect">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> rate was 19th highest in the world, estimated in 2012 at 3.20% among adults aged 15–49 years.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG/220px-Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG/330px-Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG/440px-Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2664" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A9_Abidjan_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_campus" title="University campus" class="mw-redirect">University campus</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Cocody" title="Université de Cocody" class="mw-redirect">Université de Cocody</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ivory_Coast" title="Education in Ivory Coast">Education in Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>A large part of the adult population, in particular women, are <a href="/wiki/Illiterate" title="Illiterate" class="mw-redirect">illiterate</a>. Many children between 6 and 10 years are not enrolled in school. <sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of students in secondary education are male.<sup id="cite_ref-education.stateuniversity.com_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-education.stateuniversity.com-86"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of secondary education, students can sit the Baccalauréat examination.<sup id="cite_ref-education.stateuniversity.com_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-education.stateuniversity.com-86"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The country has universities in Abidjan (<a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Cocody" title="Université de Cocody" class="mw-redirect">Université de Cocody</a>) and Bouaké (<a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Bouak%C3%A9" title="Université de Bouaké" class="mw-redirect">Université de Bouaké</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Culture of Ivory Coast">Culture of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ivory_Coast" title="Music of Ivory Coast">Music of Ivory Coast</a></div>
<p>Each of the ethnic groups in Ivory Coast has its own music genres, most showing strong vocal <a href="/wiki/Polyphony" title="Polyphony">polyphony</a>. <a href="/wiki/Talking_drum" title="Talking drum">Talking drums</a> are also common, especially among the <a href="/wiki/Nzema_people" title="Nzema people">Appolo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polyrhythm" title="Polyrhythm">polyrhythms</a>, another African characteristic, are found throughout Ivory Coast and are especially common in the southwest.</p>
<p>Popular music genres from Ivory Coast include <a href="/wiki/Zoblazo" title="Zoblazo">zoblazo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zouglou" title="Zouglou">zouglou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9-D%C3%A9cal%C3%A9" title="Coupé-Décalé">Coupé-Décalé</a>. A few Ivorian artists who have known international success are <a href="/wiki/Magic_System" title="Magic System">Magic Système</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Blondy" title="Alpha Blondy">Alpha Blondy</a>, Meiway, Dobet Gnahore, Tiken Dja Fakoly, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Goh" title="Christina Goh">Christina Goh</a> from Ivorian descent.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_at_the_Olympics" title="Ivory Coast at the Olympics">Ivory Coast at the Olympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg/300px-Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg/450px-Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg/600px-Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cote_d%27Iviore_NT_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<center>The <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast national football team</a></center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The country has been host for several major African sporting events, with the most recent being the <a href="/wiki/2013_African_Basketball_Championship" title="2013 African Basketball Championship" class="mw-redirect">2013 African Basketball Championship</a>. In the past, the country further hosted the <a href="/wiki/1984_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1984 Africa Cup of Nations" class="mw-redirect">1984 Africa Cup of Nations</a>, in which its <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire_national_football_team" title="Côte d'Ivoire national football team" class="mw-redirect">football team</a> finished 5th, and the <a href="/wiki/1985_African_Basketball_Championship" title="1985 African Basketball Championship" class="mw-redirect">1985 African Basketball Championship</a>, where its <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire_national_basketball_team" title="Côte d'Ivoire national basketball team" class="mw-redirect">basketball team</a> won the gold medal.</p>
<p>Ivory Coast won an Olympic silver medal for <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1984_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_400_metres" title="Athletics at the 1984 Summer Olympics – Men's 400 metres">men's 400-metre</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 games</a>, where it competed as "Côte d'Ivoire".</p>
<p>The most popular sport in Ivory Coast is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire_national_football_team" title="Côte d'Ivoire national football team" class="mw-redirect">national football team</a> has played in the World Cup three times, in Germany 2006, in South Africa 2010 and in Brazil in 2014. Ivory Coast notable footballers are <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaya_Tour%C3%A9" title="Yaya Touré">Yaya Touré</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gervinho" title="Gervinho">Gervinho</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is also popular, and the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire_national_rugby_union_team" title="Côte d'Ivoire national rugby union team" class="mw-redirect">national rugby union team</a> qualified to play at the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a> in South Africa in 1995.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yassapoulet.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Yassapoulet.JPG/220px-Yassapoulet.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Yassapoulet.JPG/330px-Yassapoulet.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Yassapoulet.JPG/440px-Yassapoulet.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yassapoulet.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Yassa_(food)" title="Yassa (food)">Yassa</a> is a popular dish throughout West Africa prepared with chicken or fish. Chicken yassa is pictured.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ivorian_cuisine" title="Ivorian cuisine">Ivorian cuisine</a></div>
<p>The traditional cuisine of Ivory Coast is very similar to that of neighboring countries in west Africa in its reliance on grains and <a href="/wiki/Tuber" title="Tuber">tubers</a>. Cassava and <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)" class="mw-redirect">plantains</a> are significant parts of Ivorian cuisine. A type of corn paste called "Aitiu" is used to prepare corn balls, and <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a> are widely used in many dishes. <a href="/wiki/Atti%C3%A9k%C3%A9" title="Attiéké">Attiéké</a> is a popular side dish in Ivory Coast made with grated <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> and is a vegetable-based <a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">couscous</a>. A common street-vended food is <a href="/wiki/Aloko" title="Aloko" class="mw-redirect">aloko</a>, which is ripe banana fried in <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>, spiced with steamed onions and chili and eaten alone or with grilled fish. Chicken is commonly consumed, and has a unique flavor due to its lean, low-fat mass in this region. Seafood includes <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sardine" title="Sardine">sardines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonito" title="Bonito">bonito</a>, which are similar to tuna. Mafé is a common dish consisting of meat in a <a href="/wiki/Peanut_sauce" title="Peanut sauce">peanut sauce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eats_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eats-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Slow-simmered <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a> with various ingredients are another common food staple in Ivory Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-eats_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eats-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> "Kedjenou" is a dish consisting of chicken and vegetables that are slow-cooked in a sealed pot with little or no added liquid, which concentrates the flavors of the chicken and vegetables and tenderizes the chicken.<sup id="cite_ref-eats_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eats-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> It is usually cooked in a pottery jar called a canary, over a slight fire, or cooked in an oven.<sup id="cite_ref-eats_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eats-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> "Bangui" is a local palm wine.</p>
<p>Ivorians have a particular kind of small, open-air restaurant called a maquis, which is unique to the region. Maquis normally feature braised chicken and fish covered in onions and tomatoes, served with attiéké, or <a href="/wiki/Kedjenou" title="Kedjenou">kedjenou</a>, a chicken dish made with vegetables and a mild sauce.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivory_Coast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-teeths-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-teeths_17-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Vaiss%C3%A8te" title="Joseph Vaissète">Joseph Vaissète</a>, in his 1755 <i>Géographie historique, ecclésiastique et civile</i>, lists the name as <i>La Côte des Dents</i> ("The Coast of the Teeth") but notes that <i>Côte de Dents</i> is the more correct form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVaiss.C3.A8te1755185.E2.80.93186_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVaiss.C3.A8te1755185.E2.80.93186-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-vent-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-vent_21-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Côte du Vent</i> sometimes denoted the combined "Ivory" and "Grain" coasts, or sometimes just the "Grain" coast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDuckett1853594_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDuckett1853594-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThornton199653.E2.80.9356_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThornton199653.E2.80.9356-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-trans-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-trans_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Literal translations include <i>Elfenbeinküste</i> (German), <i>Costa d'Avoria</i> (Italian), <i>Norsunluuraniko</i> (Finnish), <i>Бе́рег Слоно́вой Ко́сти</i> (Russian), and of course <i>Ivory Coast</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavid20007_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavid20007-23"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-outlets-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-outlets_30-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> usually uses "Ivory Coast" both in news reports and on its page about the country.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> newspaper's style guide says: "Ivory Coast, not 'The Ivory Coast' or 'Côte d'Ivoire'; its nationals are Ivorians."<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="background-color: #fff9f9; color: DarkSlateGray; border: 1px solid #ffdcdc;"><a href="/wiki/ABC_News_(USA)" title="ABC News (USA)" class="mw-redirect">ABC News</a>, <a href="/wiki/FOX_News" title="FOX News" class="mw-redirect">FOX News</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="South African Broadcasting Corporation">South African Broadcasting Corporation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/CBC_News" title="CBC News">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation</a> all use "Ivory Coast" either exclusively or predominantly..</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-organizations-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-organizations_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Many governments use "Côte d'Ivoire" for diplomatic reasons, as do their outlets, such as the Chinese CCTV News. <span class="citation-needed-content" style="background-color: #fff9f9; color: DarkSlateGray; border: 1px solid #ffdcdc;">Other organizations that use "Côte d'Ivoire" include <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC</a> (referring to their <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire_national_football_team" title="Côte d'Ivoire national football team" class="mw-redirect">national football</a> and Olympic teams in international games and in official broadcasts),</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> newsmagazine.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic Society</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> both use Cote d'Ivoire.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-BOLPY-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BOLPY_79-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is actually a basilica, but is listed in the <i>Guinness World Records</i> as the largest "church" in the world.</span></li>
</ol>
